It started with puberty, I am not talking growth spurts, I mean full on turning into an adult NOW  with total body changes happening....which means LOTS of hormones.&lt;br /&gt;Which is why the science of the above referenced site made sense to us as a possible cause.&lt;br /&gt;There is the difference in what kind of acne one is dealing with and how each body handles the interaction of the hormones or androgens with the skin&#x27;s normal growth cycle.&lt;br /&gt;If normal washing and zit creams don&#x27;t work for you, you may have a deeper reason for acne.&lt;br /&gt;Some people have the propensity for androgens to  interfere with the normal skin cycle.&lt;br /&gt;  That creates inflammation, which creates clogged pores, which in turn creates a prime enviorment for bacteria (pimples)to grow.&lt;br /&gt;So if you can normalize the skin cycle, the inflammation goes down which in turn, keeps acne from forming.  At least that is my non-medical take from the referenced site. Google mTor and acne.  If your body reacts a certain way, there is a cause for acne, .very interesting what they are discovering.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My teen has this kind of hormonal acne.
